    "title": "Facebook Lead Ads",
    "url": "https://www.make.com/en/help/app/facebook-lead-ads#establish-the-connection-with-facebook-lead-ads-to-make",
    "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsMarketingFacebook Lead Ads\nFacebook Lead Ads\n\nWith Facebook Lead Ads modules in Make, you can monitor leads and retrieve lead and form data from your Facebook Lead Ads account.\n\nTo use the Facebook Lead Ads modules, you must have a Facebook and a Facebook Business Manager account. You can create accounts at facebook.com and business.facebok.com.\n\nNote\n\nLearn how you can take your Facebook leads ads campaigns to the next level with Facebook Conversions API and Facebook Conversions for CRM apps. Learn more in the video here.\n\nConnect Facebook Lead Ads to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nEstablish the connection with Facebook Lead Ads to Make.\n\nAssign Make access in Facebook Business Manager\n\nNote\n\nSee our instructional video FB Lead manual and troubleshooting.\n\nEstablish the connection with Facebook Lead Ads to Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Facebook Lead Ads module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional: Click Show advanced settings and enter your custom app client credentials. For more information, refer to the Facebook Authentication Guide.\n\nIf requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/facebook.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Facebook Lead Ads modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nAssign Make access in Facebook Business Manager\n\nTo grant Make access in Facebook Business Manager:\n\nLog in to your Facebook Business Manager account.\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Settings.\n\nGo to Integrations > Leads Access.\n\nGo to CRMs, click Assign CRMs, and select Make by clicking the checkbox.\n\nClick Assign.\n\nBuild Facebook Lead Ads Scenarios\nNote\n\nYou can start with a prebuilt template or build your scenario from scratch. You can find a template for a scenario using Facebook Lead Ads and Google Sheets here.\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nLeads\n\nNew Lead\n\nNote\n\nYou can use the Lead Ads Testing Tool to test your New Lead module and see if it is receiving the form.\n\nWatch Leads\n\nGet Lead Details\n\nNote: The form you want to retrieve the data from has to have been submitted at least once before, otherwise the form won't load in the Make module.\n\nUtility\n\nGet a Form\n\nUnsubscribe a Webhook\n\nNote: Deleting a scenario will not automatically unsubscribe your Facebook Page from receiving event notifications from Facebook.\n\nOther\n\nList Leads\n\nNote\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nWhen you create a Facebook Lead Ads webhook in Make, it is attached automatically and requires no additional set up.\n\nTroubleshooting\nThe New Lead module does not trigger\nThe Make dropdown doesn't show some Facebook pages:\nThe Scenario does not start after submitting a form\n400: GraphMethodException (100): Unsupported get request.\nOAuthException (200)\nFacebook Lead Ads\nConnect Facebook Lead Ads to Make\nEstablish the connection with Facebook Lead Ads to Make\nAssign Make access in Facebook Business Manager\nBuild Facebook Lead Ads Scenarios\nTroubleshooting\nThe New Lead module does not trigger\nThe Make dropdown doesn't show some Facebook pages:\nThe Scenario does not start after submitting a form\n400: GraphMethodException (100): Unsupported get request.\nOAuthException (200)\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

    "title": "Facebook Conversions API for CRM",
    "url": "https://www.make.com/en/help/app/facebook-conversion-leads#connect-facebook-conversions-api-for-crm-tomake",
    "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsMarketingFacebook Conversions API for CRM\nFacebook Conversions API for CRM\n\nWith the Facebook Conversion API for CRM modules in Make, you can create lead events.\n\nTo get started with the Facebook Conversions API for CRM app:\n\ncreate a Facebook account\n\ncreate a Facebook Business Manager account at business.facebook.com\n\ncreate a new pixel specifically for the lead events in your Facebook Event Manager. The pixel should be of type CRM.\n\nstart sending simple \"Lead\" events with the Facebook Conversions API app immediately after you receive leads with Facebook Leads Ads app. More info can be found in the video below.\n\nstart sending lead status change events via Make to Facebook with the Facebook Conversions API for CRM app. The Facebook account used during the connection creation should be the admin of the Facebook Ads account and the newly created pixel.\n\nafter a week or so, you need to go to the Pixel's Settings and finish the configuration of your sales funnel to define the lead status that will be used for optimizing your Facebook Lead Ads Campaigns where the optimization is set to Facebook Conversions API for CRM.\n\nMake strongly recommends watching the video below to understand the above prerequisites before you start using the app.\n\nNote\n\nAs mentioned in the video, in order to be able to use the Facebook Conversions API for CRM app, you first need to start capturing Facebook lead IDs in your CRM. To do so, you can start using the Facebook Lead Ads app on Make.\n\nThis app allows you to listen for new form submissions on Facebook and then pass the form data along with the Lead ID to your CRM. For more information, see the Facebook Lead Ads app.\n\nConnect Facebook Conversions API for CRM to Make\n\nTo connect to the Facebook Conversions API for CRM app:\n\nLog in to your Make account, insert a Facebook Conversions API for CRM module in your scenario, and click the Add button next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: Click Show Advanced Settings to enter the client credentials of your custom application.\n\nAdd the details as provided below to connect the app:\n\nConnection name\n\n\t\n\nOptional: Enter a name for the connection.\n\n\n\n\nYour Business Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter your business name.\n\n\n\n\nCurrency\n\n\t\n\nSelect the applicable currency for your business. For example, USD.\n\n\n\n\nTimezone\n\n\t\n\nSelect the timezone applicable to your business.\n\n\n\n\nExternal Business ID\n\n\t\n\nOptional: Enter a unique Business ID.\n\nNote\n\nMake strongly recommends entering an External Business ID as a unique identifier to distinguish multiple businesses.\n\nThis field is mandatory if you want to create multiple connections to multiple Facebook Business accounts.\n\nThe ID can be any string of your choice but ensure the ID is unique for your different businesses if you run more than one business.\n\nFor example, fubar-123 is for a business called Fubar.\n\n\n\n\nClient ID and Client Secret\n\n\t\n\nOptional: Client credentials of your custom application.\n\nClick Save and select your account settings for the connection.\n\nNote\n\nThe connection setup could take up to 3 - 5 minutes.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenarioand add more Facebook Conversions API for CRM modules. If your connection needs reauthorization, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nList of modules to start with in scenarios with the most common CRM apps\n\nStart by selecting one of the following CRM modules you want to connect to Facebook and upload lead events.\n\nThe following table provides the apps and the modules to start with these apps using Make:\n\nCRM\n\n\t\n\nModule to Start With\n\n\t\n\nNotes\n\n\n\n\nHubSpot\n\n\t\n\nWatch Records\n\n\t\n\nMonitors both creations and updates\n\n\n\n\nSalesforce\n\n\t\n\nWatch Records\n\n\t\n\nMonitors both creations and updates\n\n\n\n\nZoho\n\n\t\n\nWatch Objects\n\n\t\n\nMonitors both creations and updates\n\n\n\n\nBitrix\n\n\t\n\nWatch Leads/Deals\n\n\t\n\nThe modules should be set to watch by modified time.\n\n\n\n\nMicrosoft Dynamics\n\n\t\n\nSearch Records\n\n\t\n\nThe Watch Records will only give you creations but not updates, so you will have to go with search and filter for records that have been edited since the last run.\n\nActions\n\nYou can create events with the following module.\n\nCreate a Lead Event\n\nCreates a specific lead.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Facebook Conversions API for CRM account.\n\n\n\n\nEvent Name\n\n\t\n\nName of the event to capture the stages you use within your CRM.\n\nEnsure to send all stages as they are updated, including the initial lead stage.\n\nFor example, your stages may include the following types.\n\nIf a lead reaches the final, Converted stage, all previous stages should have been sent beforehand.\n\nInitial Lead from FB\n\nMarketing Qualified Lead\n\nSales Opportunity\n\nConverted\n\nFacebook recommends using a variable to pass in the stages from your database. Alternatively, you could create a separate API call for each stage.\n\n\n\n\nEvent Time\n\n\t\n\nA timestamp that indicates when your CRM updates the lead stage update event.\n\nFacebook recommends using a variable to pass in the Unix timestamp values from your database.\n\nNote\n\nThe event_time parameter value can be up to 7 days before you send an event to Facebook.\n\n\n\n\nLead ID\n\n\t\n\nThe FB generated ID for every lead, a 15 or 16-digit number.\n\nIt is required to use Lead IDs instead of customer information for matching. Facebook recommends using a variable to pass in the ID values from your database.\n\nLead ID associated with a lead generated by Facebook's Lead Ads. This means you can only use this module when your lead originally came from Lead Ads, and you saved its Lead ID.\n\n\n\n\nLead Event Source\n\n\t\n\nName of the tool where the leads are coming from.\n\nWe suggest you use Make or anything regarding your business process. You can also use the name of the true source system. For example, CRMs such as Hubspot, Salesforce, Pipedrive, etc.,\n\n\n\n\nPixel ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Pixel ID of your Facebook account. To create and set up the Pixel ID, refer to Facebook help page.\n\nLeave this field empty for the pixel ID you picked when creating or reauthorizing the connection. If you want a pixel under a different Facebook Business Manager account, create a new connection instead.\n\nFor more information, see the Facebook Conversions API for CRM Integration page.\n\nFacebook Conversions API for CRM\nConnect Facebook Conversions API for CRM to Make\nList of modules to start with in scenarios with the most common CRM apps\nActions\nCreate a Lead Event\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityTSheets\nTSheets\nGetting Started with TSheets\n\nThe TSheets modules allow you to watch, create, update, list, retrieve, and delete the timesheets, users, notifications, files, invitations, jobs/customers, reminders, groups, and clients in your TSheets account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA TSheets account\n\nIn order to use TSheets with Make, it is necessary to have a TSheets account. If you do not have one, you can create a TSheets account at www.tsheets.com/signup-int.\n\nConnecting TSheets to Make\n\nTo connect your TSheets account to Make, you need to obtain the Client ID and Client Secret from your TSheets account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your TSheets account.\n\n2. From the Dashboard, click Feature Add-ons > Manage Add-ons.\n\n3. Scroll down to API and click Install.\n\n5. Click Add New Application.\n\n6. Enter the details of the app similar to the following screen and click Save.\n\nIn the OAuth Redirect URI field, enter the URI as https://www.integromat.com/oAuth/cb/tsheets.\n\n7. You can find the Client ID and Client Secret details in the API Application Details section. Copy the values to your clipboard.\n\n8. To save the application details with a token, click Save.\n\n9. Go to Make and open the TSheets module's Create a Connection dialog.\n\n10. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n11. In the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the Client ID and Client Secret copied in step 7, respectively.\n\n12. Click Continue.\n\n13. Confirm the access by clicking Allow.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTimesheets\nWatch Timesheets\nList Timesheets\nGet a Timesheet\nCreate a Timesheet\nUpdate a Timesheet\nDelete a Timesheet\nJobs/Customers\nList Jobs/Customers\nGet a Job/Customer\nCreate a Job/Customer\nUpdate a Job/Customer\nUsers\nList Users\nGet a User\nCreate a User\nUpdate a User\nReminders\nWatch Reminders\nList Reminders\nCreate a Reminder\nUpdate a Reminder\nGroups\nList Groups\nCreate a Group\nUpdate a Group\nInvitations\nCreate an Invitation\nManaged Clients\nList Managed Clients\nNotifications\nList Notifications\nCreate a Notification\nDelete a Notification\nFiles\nWatch Files\nList Files\nDownload a File\nUpdate a File\nDelete a File\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Jobs/Customers\nTSheets\nGetting Started with TSheets\nConnecting TSheets to Make\nTimesheets\nWatch Timesheets\nList Timesheets\nGet a Timesheet\nCreate a Timesheet\nUpdate a Timesheet\nDelete a Timesheet\nJobs/Customers\nList Jobs/Customers\nGet a Job/Customer\nCreate a Job/Customer\nUpdate a Job/Customer\nUsers\nList Users\nGet a User\nCreate a User\nUpdate a User\nReminders\nWatch Reminders\nList Reminders\nCreate a Reminder\nUpdate a Reminder\nGroups\nList Groups\nCreate a Group\nUpdate a Group\nInvitations\nCreate an Invitation\nManaged Clients\nList Managed Clients\nNotifications\nList Notifications\nCreate a Notification\nDelete a Notification\nFiles\nWatch Files\nList Files\nDownload a File\nUpdate a File\nDelete a File\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Jobs/Customers\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

For subscription information and creating an account, refer to the Gravity Forms Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the Gravity Forms API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Gravity Forms to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your Consumer Key and Consumer Secret in WordPress.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your Consumer Key and Consumer Secret in WordPress\n\nTo obtain your API key from your WordPress account:\n\nLog in to your WordPress account where you use the Gravity Forms plugin.\n\nGo to Formsand open Settings.\n\nGo to REST API.\n\nUnder REST API Settings, select Enable access to the API.\n\nUnder Authentication ( API version 2 ), click Add Key.\n\nIn the Add New Key window, do the following:\n\nOptional: Enter a description of the API key.\n\nIn the Permissions drop-down list, select Read/Write.\n\nClick Add.\n\nCopy your Consumer Key and Consumer Secret values and store them in a safe place.\n\nYou will use these values in the Consumer Key and Consumer Secret fields in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Gravity Forms module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Consumer Key and Consumer Secret fields, enter the credentials copied in the section above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Gravity Forms modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Gravity Forms Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTriggers\n\nWatch Entries\n\nActions\n\nRemove a Feed\n\nNote: The Feed ID can be retrieved using the List Feeds module.\n\nGet Form Results\n\nNote: The Feed ID can be retrieved using the List Feeds module.\n\nGet an Entry\n\nGet a Form\n\nRemove an Entry\n\nRemove a Form\n\nMake an API Call\n\nSearches\n\nList Entries of a Form\n\nList Entries\n\nList Feeds\n\nList Forms\n\nGravity Forms\nConnect Gravity Forms to Make\nObtain your Consumer Key and Consumer Secret in WordPress\nEstablish the connection in Make\nBuild Gravity Forms Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

    "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and ERPs\nCommerce\nCommunication\nCRM and Sales tools\nCustomer Support\nDatabase\nEducation\nFile and Document Management\nHR management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nCloudflare\nBlogger\ncoreBos\nCraftQL\nElementor\nGhost\nMedium\nNetlify\nSimvoly\nSquarespace\nTilda\nUnbounce\nWebflow\nWix\nWordPress\nWordPress (legacy)\nWP All Import\nWP Webhooks\nYoast\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsWebsite BuildingWordPress (legacy)\nWordPress (legacy)\n\nVersion Legacy\n\nNote\n\nThis is the documentation for the legacy WordPress app. Here is the documentation for the new WordPress app.\n\nGetting Started with WordPress\n\nThe Wordpress modules allow you to monitor, publish, update, delete, or search posts, pages, comments, media, users, and tags on your Wordpress site.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nWordpress installed on your server\n\nA Basic Authentication for JSON plugin installed in your Wordpress\n\nModified .htaccess or web.config file (optional)\n\nCustom Fields for REST API plugin (optional, for working with custom fields)\n\nIn order to use Wordpress with Make, it is necessary to have the Wordpress content management system installed on your server or webhosting. You can download Wordpress at wordpress.org/download/ and install by following the instructions on wordpress.org/support/article/how-to-install-wordpress.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting WordPress to Make\n\nTo connect your WordPress account to Make, the JSON Basic Auth plugin has to be installed in your WordPress installation.\n\nVisit github.com/WP-API/Basic-Auth and download the JSON Basic Authentication plugin (direct link).\n\nLog in to your WordPress administration and open Plugins.\n\nClick the Add New button.\n\nClick on the Upload plugin button, browse and select the plugin ZIP file.\n\nClick on the Install now button to install the plugin.\n\nAfter the installation is finished, click on the Activate Plugin button.\n\nGo to Make and open the Create a connection dialog of the desired WordPress module. Enter the URL of your WordPress site and your WordPress credentials to the respective fields.\n\nEstablish a connection by clicking the Continue button.\n\nWarning\n\nIf the connection is not established and an error is returned, you need to add the following code to your .htaccessfile to allow the HTTP authorization header:\n\n<IfModule mod_setenvif>\n\nSetEnvIf Authorization \"(.*)\" HTTP_AUTHORIZATION=$1 \n\n</IfModule>\n\nIf your WordPress is on the Windows server (IIS), please contact your administrator in order to allow the HTTP authorization header.\n\nAdd the Self-signed Certificate When Using Secured HTTPS Connection\n\nSelf-signed certificate\n\n\t\n\nClick the Extract button to open the upload dialog.\n\nUpload the certificate to use the TLS with your self-signed certificate. Make does not retain or store any data (files, passwords) you provide. File and password are only used to extract the certificate.\n\nFor more details about certificates and keys please refer to the Certificates and Keys article.\n\nCustom Fields for REST API plugin installation\n\nVisit https://wordpress.org/plugins/rest-api-custom-fields/ and download the Custom Fields for REST API plugin (direct link).\n\nLog in to your Wordpress administration and open Plugins.\n\nClick the Add New button.\n\nClick on the Upload plugin button, browse and select the plugin ZIP file.\n\nClick on the Install now button to install the plugin.\n\nAfter the installation is finished, click on the Activate Plugin button.\n\nFollow these instructions in order to add a custom field to your post, page, media, or another object.\n\nGo to Settings and open the Rest API Custom Fields dialog.\n\nSelect the desired object's custom fields you want to include in the REST API response.\n\nClick on the Save Settings button.\n\nThe selected custom fields are now available in the module response.\n\nPosts\nWatch Posts\nCreate a Post\nUpdate a Post\nDelete a Post\nGet a Post\nSearch for a Post\nPages\nWatch pages\nCreate a Page\nUpdate a page\nDelete a Page\nGet a Page\nSearch for a Page\nCategories\nWatch Categories\nCreate a Category\nUpdate a Category\nDelete a Category\nGet a Category\nSearch for a Category\nComments\nWatch Comments\nCreate a Comment\nUpdate a Comment\nDelete a Comment\nGet a Comment\nSearch for a Comment\nMedia\nWatch Media Items\nCreate a Media Item\nUpdate a Media Item\nDelete Media Item\nGet a Media Item\nSearch for a Media Item\nUsers\nWatch Users\nCreate a User\nUpdate a User\nDelete a User\nGet a User\nSearch for a User\nTags\nWatch Tags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nGet a Tag\nSearch for a Tag\nOther\nGet My Info\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Pages\nWordPress (legacy)\nGetting Started with WordPress\nConnecting WordPress to Make\nAdd the Self-signed Certificate When Using Secured HTTPS Connection\nCustom Fields for REST API plugin installation\nPosts\nWatch Posts\nCreate a Post\nUpdate a Post\nDelete a Post\nGet a Post\nSearch for a Post\nPages\nWatch pages\nCreate a Page\nUpdate a page\nDelete a Page\nGet a Page\nSearch for a Page\nCategories\nWatch Categories\nCreate a Category\nUpdate a Category\nDelete a Category\nGet a Category\nSearch for a Category\nComments\nWatch Comments\nCreate a Comment\nUpdate a Comment\nDelete a Comment\nGet a Comment\nSearch for a Comment\nMedia\nWatch Media Items\nCreate a Media Item\nUpdate a Media Item\nDelete Media Item\nGet a Media Item\nSearch for a Media Item\nUsers\nWatch Users\nCreate a User\nUpdate a User\nDelete a User\nGet a User\nSearch for a User\nTags\nWatch Tags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nGet a Tag\nSearch for a Tag\nOther\nGet My Info\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Log in to your Simvoly account.\n\n2. Click Settings > Applications.\n\n3. Copy the API Key to your clipboard.\n\n4. Log in to your Make account and add a module from the Simvoly app into an Make scenario.\n\n5. Click Add next to the Connection field.\n\n6. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n7. In the Domain field, enter your account URL address. For example, https://example.simvoly.com.\n\n8. In the API Key field, enter the API key copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nContact\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in Simvoly once you add an instant trigger to your scenario.\n\nWatch Contact Activities\n\nTriggers when a new contact is created or an existing contact is updated.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\nWatch Contacts\n\nTriggers when a new contact is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of contacts Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nList Contacts\n\nRetrieves a list of contacts.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nCreated at Minimum\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the date and time to list the contacts that were created on or after the specified time. product options. Leave this field blank empty if quantity is not tracked.\n\n\n\n\nSKU\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the product Stock Keeping Unit number.\n\n\n\n\nWeight\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the product weight.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the product details.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the product URL address in your store.\n\n\n\n\nHidden\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether the product is visible in your store.\n\n\n\n\nImages\n\n\t\n\nAdd the image URL address of the product.\n\n\n\n\nCategories\n\n\t\n\nAdd the product categories:\n\nCategory ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Category ID of the product.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the category name.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the category URL address in the store.\n\n\n\n\nParent Category\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Parent Category ID of this category. Enter 0 if this is the root category.\n\n\n\n\nOptions\n\n\t\n\nAdd the options for the product:\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the option. For example, color, size, material.\n\n\n\n\nValues\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the values of the options. For example, for size, it is small, medium, and large.\n\n\n\n\nAdvanced\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether different variations of the options have different prices, quantities, SKU, or weights tracked.\n\n\n\n\nSubscription\n\n\t\n\nAdd the subscription details of the product:\n\nCycles\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the number of payment cycles. Enter 0 for ongoing payments, and a positive integer for a fixed number of payments.\n\n\n\n\nPeriod\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the number showing the subscription period. For example, every 1 month, 2 months, 1 week, etc.\n\n\n\n\nUnit\n\n\t\n\nEnter the subscription validity:\n\nWeekly\n\nMonthly\n\n\n\n\nFile\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the digital file details if the product you are selling is a digital product.\n\n\n\n\nUpdate Existing Product by URL\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether if this is an existing product. If the product is existing then the details will be updated.\n\nUpdate a Product\n\nUpdates an existing product.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nProduct ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Product ID whose details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the product name.\n\n\n\n\nVariants\n\n\t\n\nAdd the product variant details:\n\nOptions\n\n\t\n\nAdd the product options. Created\n\nTriggers when a new order is created.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\nWatch Order Updated\n\nTriggers when a new order is updated.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\nWatch Orders\n\nTriggers when a new order is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of orders Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nList Orders\n\nRetrieves a list of orders.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nCreated at Minimum\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the connection to your Simvoly account.\n\nWatch Form Submissions\n\nTriggers when a form is submitted.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Simvoly account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://developmentpeoly.simvoly.com For example: /api/site/member-groups\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Simvoly API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGETto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOSTto create a new entry.\n\nPUTto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCHto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETEto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Orders\n\nThe following API call returns all the orders from your Simvoly account:\n\nURL:/api/site/orders\n\nMethod:GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > items. Webhook URL, Webhook Name and Webhook API Key\n\nGo to Make and open the WB Webhooks module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nEnter the values that you found in step 3 to the respective fields and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established and you can proceed to set up the module.\n\nWebhook Action\n\nUse this module to send data to your Wordpress.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your WP Webhooks plugin.\n\n\n\n\nWebhook Action\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name of the action you want to perform using the module.\n\nYou must activate desired actions first. It can be done under:\n\nSettings > WP Webhooks > Settings:\n\n\n\n\nArguments\n\n\t\n\nEnter the argument and value.\n\nThe list of arguments for each action can be found under:\n\nSettings > WP Webhooks > Receive Data > Available Webhook Actions\n\nExample - Create a User:\n\nWebhook Action\n\ncreate_user\n\nArguments\n\nArgument\n\n\t\n\nuser_mail\n\n\n\n\nValue\n\n\t\n\nemail address of the new email\n\nWP Webhooks\nGetting Started with WP Webhooks\nConnecting WP Webhooks to Make\nWebhook Action\nExample - Create a User:\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

    "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and ERPs\nCommerce\nCommunication\nCRM and Sales tools\nCustomer Support\nDatabase\nEducation\nFile and Document Management\nHR management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nCloudflare\nBlogger\ncoreBos\nCraftQL\nElementor\nGhost\nMedium\nNetlify\nSimvoly\nSquarespace\nTilda\nUnbounce\nWebflow\nWix\nWordPress\nWordPress (legacy)\nWP All Import\nWP Webhooks\nYoast\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsWebsite BuildingNetlify\nNetlify\n\nThe Netlify modules enable you to monitor form submissions, deploy events, deploy starts, deploy success and deploy failures, or retrieve sites and start deploys in your Netlify account.\n\nGetting Started with Netlify\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Netlify account\n\nIn order to use Netlify with Make, it is necessary to have a Netlify account. If you do not have one, you can create a Netlify account at Netlify.\n\nConnecting Netlify to Make\n\nTo connect your Netlify account to Make you need to obtain the access token from your Netlify account.\n\n1. Log in to your Netlify account.\n\n2. Click on your profile icon and select the User settings option.\n\n3. Open Applications and click New access token.\n\n4. Enter the description for the access token and click the Generate token button.\n\n5. Copy the provided token and close the dialog by clicking the Done button.\n\n6. Go to Make and open the Netlify module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n7. Enter the Access Token you have copied in step 5 to the respective field and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nSite\nWatch Form Submissions\n\nTriggers when a new form is submitted on the specified site.\n\nNetlify comes with built-in form handling. The build bots do it by parsing your HTML files directly at deploy time, so there's no need for you to make an API call or include extra JavaScript on your site. For more information, you can view the documentation on https://docs.netlify.com/forms/setup/#html-forms.\n\nCode an HTML form into any page on your site, add a netlify attribute or data-netlify=\"true\" to the <form> tag, and you can start receiving submissions in your Netlify site admin panel.\n\nHere's an example:\n\n<form name=\"contact\" method=\"POST\" data-netlify=\"true\">\n  <p>\n    <label>Your Name: <input type=\"text\" name=\"name\" /></label>   \n  </p>\n  <p>\n    <label>Your Email: <input type=\"email\" name=\"email\" /></label>\n  </p>\n  <p>\n    <label>Your Role: <select name=\"role[]\" multiple>\n      <option value=\"leader\">Leader</option>\n      <option value=\"follower\">Follower</option>\n    </select></label>\n  </p>\n  <p>\n    <label>Message: <textarea name=\"message\"></textarea></label>\n  </p>\n  <p>\n    <button type=\"submit\">Send</button>\n  </p>\n</form>\n\nTo create the webhook for Watch Form Submissions module follow the steps below:\n\n1. Choose the Watch Form Submissions module.\n\n2. Add a new webhook.\n\n3. Fill the Add a hook dialog as follows:\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site that contains the form you want to watch for new form submissions.\n\n\n\n\nForm ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the form you want to watch for new form submissions.\n\nList Sites\n\nLists sites deployed on your Netlify account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the site name to filter results by. Otherwise, all your sites deployed on Netlify will be returned. E.g. elastic-keller-f19a9b.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of sites Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet a Site\n\nRetrieves details about a specified site.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site name or map the ID of the site you want to retrieve details about.\n\nSite Deploy\nWatch Deploy Events\n\nTriggers when a selected deploy event occurs.\n\nTo create the webhook for Watch Deploy Events module follow the steps below:\n\n1. Choose the Watch Deploy Events module.\n\n2. Add a new webhook.\n\n3. Fill the Add a hook dialog as follows:\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to watch for new deploy events.\n\n\n\n\nEvent\n\n\t\n\nSelect the event you want to watch.\n\nDeploy request pending: Emitted when an untrusted deploy requires approval to begin building, as specified by the site's sensitive variable policy.\n\nDeploy request accepted: Emitted when an untrusted deploy request is accepted and can begin building.\n\nDeploy request rejected: Emitted when an untrusted deploy request is rejected.\n\nDeploy building: Emitted when Netlify starts building your site for a new deploy.\n\nDeploy created: Emitted when Netlify finishes uploading a new deploy to our CDN.\n\nDeploy failed: Emitted when a deploy does not complete.\n\nDeploy locked: Emitted when the site is locked to a published deploy, stopping auto-publishing.\n\nDeploy unlocked: Emitted when deploys are unlocked, resuming auto-publishing.\n\nWatch Deploy Start\n\nTriggers when a new deploy starts for a specified website.\n\nTo create the webhook for Watch Deploy Start module follow the steps below:\n\n1. Choose the Watch Deploy Start module.\n\n2. Add a new webhook.\n\n3. Fill the Add a hook dialog as follows:\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to watch for new deploy starts.\n\nWatch Deploy Success\n\nTriggers when a new deploy succeeds for a specified website.\n\nTo create the webhook for Watch Deploy Success module follow the steps below:\n\n1. Choose the Watch Deploy Success module.\n\n2. Add a new webhook.\n\n3. Fill the Add a hook dialog as follows:\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to watch for new deploy successes.\n\nWatch Deploy Failure\n\nTriggers when a new deploy fails for a specified website.\n\nTo create the webhook for Watch Deploy Failure module follow the steps below:\n\n1. Choose the Watch Deploy Failure module.\n\n2. Add a new webhook.\n\n3. Fill the Add a hook dialog as follows:\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to watch for new deploy failures.\n\nList Site Deploys\n\nRetrieves all site deploys.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to retrieve deploys for.\n\nCreate Site Deploy\n\nCreates a deploy for the specified site.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site you want to create a deploy for.\n\n\n\n\nDeploy title\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the deploy.\n\n\n\n\nDraft\n\n\t\n\nCheck this option to create a draft.\n\n\n\n\nAsync\n\n\t\n\nRequests that last longer than 30 seconds will be terminated automatically. When creating large deploys, check the Async option.\n\nSite Build\nStart a Deploy\n\nStarts a new deploy on a specified site.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site or map the ID of the site you want to start the deploy for.\n\nFile\nList Files\n\nReturns a list of all files in the current deploy.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nSite ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the site or map the ID of the site you want to return a list of files for.\n\nOther\nMake an API Call\n\nAllows you to perform a custom API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Netlify account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.netlify.com/apie.g./v1/sites.\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Netlify API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOSTto create a new entry.\n\nPUT to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCHto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETEto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery string\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Site Deploys\n\nThe following API call returns all the deploys for the specified site in your Netlify account:\n\nURL: /v1/sites/{{yourSiteID}}/deploys/v1/dashboard\n\nMethod: GET\n\nThe result can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body. In our example, 3 deploys were returned:\n\nNetlify\nGetting Started with Netlify\nConnecting Netlify to Make\nSite\nWatch Form Submissions\nList Sites\nGet a Site\nSite Deploy\nWatch Deploy Events\nWatch Deploy Start\nWatch Deploy Success\nWatch Deploy Failure\nList Site Deploys\nCreate Site Deploy\nSite Build\nStart a Deploy\nFile\nList Files\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Site Deploys\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

    "title": "Glossary",
    "url": "https://www.make.com/en/help/glossary#content-wrapper",
    "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterGlossary\nGlossary\nACID\n\nACID stands for atomicity, consistency, isolation, and durability. These four properties guarantee database accuracy and stability during transactions. See this article for more information.\n\nMake marks this functionality with a badge. Note that the ACID badge indicates the use of these properties and does not indicate whether the module is an instant or polling trigger.\n\nAction module\n\nYou can create, read, update, or delete data with an action module. Action modules are the most common type of module and can be at the beginning, middle, or end of a scenario. There is no limit to the number of action modules in your scenario.\n\nActive and inactive scenarios\n\nThere are two ways you can use scenarios in Make depending on how you want your scenario to function:\n\nActive scenarios run according to a defined schedule or webhook.\n\nFor example: to watch a spreadsheet or webhook.\n\nInactive scenarios execute manually whenever you wish to run them.\n\nFor example: limited, one-time results such as retrieving data for a specific time.\n\nYou can change between active and inactive whenever you like on the Scenarios tab.\n\nAggregator\n\nAn aggregator is a type of module that allows you to merge multiple bundles into one single bundle. Aggregators are useful in making data readable for certain modules or generating meaningful output. Make offers:\n\nArray aggregator\n\nNumerical aggregator\n\nTable aggregator\n\nText aggregator\n\nSee Also Aggregator article.\n\nArray\n\nWithin a bundle, data items of the same type are sometimes in an array. You can find an array by looking at the details of a bundle.\n\nDepending on the details of your scenario, you can map other modules to a specific item in an array or use iterators and aggregators to manipulate your data into other formats.\n\nWhen mapping, Make marks arrays with [ ].\n\nArray aggregator\n\nWhen designing a scenario, use an array aggregator to merge multiple bundles into one single bundle. This may be necessary to format data properly for subsequent modules. The array aggregator also lets you define your target data structure.\n\nSee Also Aggregator article.\n\nAuto commit\n\nThe Auto commit option defines how Make process data transactions. Enabling Auto commit switches all operations to the commit phase. In the case of an error, data commits immediately and you cannot restore any lost data.\n\nNote\n\nIf you disable Auto commit, no commit occurs until operations are executed for all modules. Only modules with the \"ACID\" tag support transactionality.\n\nSee Also Scenario execution, cycles, and phases article.\n\nBlueprint\n\nMake lets you import and export scenarios via a blueprint, a file in JSON format. Your blueprint contains all of your modules and settings except for connections. When importing from a blueprint, you must add your connections.\n\nNote\n\nBlueprints are not compatible between Integromat and Make.\n\nBreak error handling directive\n\nUsing a break directive lets you resolve errors manually and helps when you want more human oversight of errors. When an error occurs, the break directive stops execution of subsequent modules and stores the error in the queue of incomplete executions. Then, the break directive creates a separate record for each bundle that causes the error (available under the Incomplete executions tab > Details). Here, you can manually resolve the error and process all unprocessed bundles. The scenario execution history shows the status as Warning.\n\nNote\n\nYou must enable storing of incomplete executions under Scenario settings.\n\nBundle\n\nA bundle is a chunk of data and the basic unit for use with modules. A bundle consists of items, similar to how a bag may contain separate, individual items.\n\nClone module\n\nWhen you need a quick duplicate of a module (for example when using data store modules on each branch of a router), use the clone module command to make an exact duplicate of your module. It appears instantly and has the same settings and variables as the original module. You can then drag it to wherever you need it and customize the settings. Changes in the original do not affect the clone and vice versa.\n\nNote\n\nYou cannot clone the trigger module of your scenario.\n\nClone scenario\n\nYou can duplicate a scenario from the Scenario tab by using the Clone option on the drop down menu for the scenario. Possible uses include sales with multiple pipelines. Use Clone scenario to create a duplicate scenario and customize for each pipeline. Changes in the original do not affect the clone and vice versa.\n\nCommit error handling directive\n\nUse the commit error handling directive when you want to stop the execution of the scenario completely but still have the sent data. When there is an error, the commit directive:\n\nstops execution immediately\n\ndoes not process the subsequent modules\n\nignores all unprocessed bundles\n\nThe scenario execution history displays the status as Success.\n\nCommit phase\n\nCommit is the third phase of a scenario execution. If the operation phase is successful for all modules, the commit phase begins and makes all data changes permanent. This means that Make sends information to all the services involved in the operation phase about its success.\n\nSee Also Scenario execution, cycles, and phases article.\n\nConnection\n\nA connection allows Make to communicate with an app/service. When adding an app/service to a Make, you may have to create a connection between Make and that app/service to retrieve or send necessary data. Make asks for only the specific permissions required. As a result, some apps/services may ask for permission multiple times. For more information, see Connecting to services\n\nConverger\n\nA converger is the counterpart to the router module and merges several routes into one route. There is no converger module available in Make, but there is a workaround, allowing you to reduce the duplication of modules in different routes.\n\nSee Also Converger workaround.\n\nCopy module\n\nWhen working with multiple scenarios, use the copy module command to create a duplicate of your module that you can paste to any scenario. It functions similar to cutting and pasting text on your computer. Although cloning a module is faster, copying allows you to paste the module in another scenario. Copying a module will also copy any filters before the original module. You can also box select (shift + drag) several modules and copy them with the ctrl + C shortcut. This is helpful when creating complex scenarios.\n\nCycle\n\nA cycle is the operation and commit/rollback phases of scenario execution. A scenario may have one or more cycles (one is the default).\n\nSee Also Cycles.\n\nData loss\n\nThe data loss option enables data to be lost if Make fails to save a bundle to the queue of incomplete executions (e.g. due to a lack of free space). Enable data loss to prevent interruptions in the overall scenario execution, e.g. a scenario where it is imperative the scenario keeps running and the incoming erroneous data is not that important.\n\nSee Also Scenario settings article.\n\nData store\n\nA data store is a built-in database in Make .You can use data stores to store data from scenarios or transfer data between individual scenarios or scenario runs. Your account includes data stores, so you do not have to register at a third-party service.\n\nData structure\n\nWhen you create a data store, you need to create a data structure that formats your data store in Make. Think of the data store as a spreadsheet and the data structure as the headers. The data structure defines the kind of data (i.e. text, numeric, etc.) that the data store records. You can view and manage your data structures from the data structures page. You can reuse your data structures.\n\nData Transfer\n\nData transfer is the amount of data transferred through your scenario.\n\nSee Also Pricing parameters.\n\nDiagram\n\nThe diagram is a visual representation of your scenario and appears exactly the same way as you see your scenario in the Scenario editor. Use the diagram tab to quickly view:\n\nthe execution history of your scenario.\n\nthe amount of operations and data consumed.\n\nthe controls to manage the scenario.\n\nDirective (error handling)\n\nA directive allows you to control how Make handles errors. There are six error handling directives:\n\nRollback\n\nCommit\n\nResume\n\nIgnore\n\nBreak\n\nRetry\n\nExplain flow\n\nThe Explain flow button allows you to see how the data will flow through from module to module before you run your scenario. Clicking the Explain flow button  starts an animated visualization of how your bundles flow through your scenario.\n\nFilter\n\nA filter helps you select bundles that fit specific criteria. You can add a filter between two modules to be sure that bundles received from the preceding modules fulfill specific conditions. Make offers:\n\nBasic operator filters\n\nText filters\n\nNumeric filters\n\nDate-time filters\n\nTime filters\n\nBoolean filters\n\nArray filters\n\nSee Also Filtering article.\n\nFinalization phase\n\nFinalization is the fourth and final phase of scenario execution. The finalization phase closes open connections (e.g. FTP connections, database connections, etc.) and marks the scenario as completed.\n\nFunctions\n\nFunctions allow you to create complex formulas when mapping items. The functions available in Make are similar to functions in Google Sheets and those in other programming languages. The functions let you perform various transformations of item values, such as converting a text to uppercase, trimming a text, converting a date into a different format, and many others. Hovering over a function gives you a brief explanation and usage example.\n\nSee Also Functions article.\n\nHistory\n\nMake maintains a history of your scenario and records:\n\nDate that scenario execution started\n\nStatus (success, warning, or error)\n\nExecution duration\n\nNumber of operations spent during the scenario run\n\nSize of transferred data\n\nLink to detailed information, where you can inspect all data in that particular execution received and how the data was processed\n\nYou can view this information by clicking on history in Scenario detail or in the Diagram. Viewing from the diagram allows you to see currently running executions and stop them if necessary.\n\nIgnore error handling directive\n\nUse the ignore error handling directive when you want a scenario to continue processing the next bundles if an error occurs. The ignore directive does not process the bundle where the error occurred through subsequent modules. The scenario execution status is marked as Success.\n\nThe ignore directive is the default when you use a module instead of an error handling directive.\n\nIncomplete executions\n\nSometimes Make cannot successfully finalize a scenario execution due to an error.\n\nMake stores incomplete executions in a folder named Incomplete Executions. Each stored incomplete execution can be resolved either manually or automatically.\n\nInitialization phase\n\nInitialization is the first phase of scenario execution. During the initialization phase, Make creates all necessary connections (for example, to databases, email services, etc.). The initialization phase also checks if each module is capable of performing its intended operation(s).\n\nInstant trigger\n\nSee Webhook.\n\nItem\n\nAn item is data that is part of a bundle. There are several different types of items: text, number, boolean (yes/no), date, time, buffer (binary data), collections, and arrays. You can find these details by clicking on the inspector at the upper-right of your module.\n\nIterator\n\nWhen creating a scenario, use an iterator to divide one bundle into smaller separate bundles. Subsequent modules then process the bundles separately. One common use is when automatically uploading email attachments to a cloud drive.\n\nYou can find iterators under Flow control of the tools section.\n\nSee Also Iterator article.\n\nKeychain\n\nThe keychain helps you to administer the keys you have stored in Make. Each key is a unique identifier used for encryption.\n\nSee Also Keys.\n\nKey (data store)\n\nWhen creating a new data store, you can assign unique identifiers to each record. Make will create a key for you if you leave the key field blank. You can also map the value of your key to make it easier to find information in your data store.\n\nMapping\n\nMapping links the modules in your scenario. When you map an item, you connected the data retrieved by one module to another module to perform the desired action. For example, you can map the email address and subject lines from the Email > Watch emails module to Google Sheets > Add a row and create a spreadsheet of email addresses and subjects.\n\nSee Also Mapping.\n\nModule\n\nModules are the main building blocks of automation in Make. Modules represent actions that Make performs with an app. Each app typically contains several modules that read, create, update, and delete data.\n\nNotes\n\nClicking the notes button  lets you add notes to your modules in your scenario. The notes feature is very useful for keeping track of webhook links. You can also use notes to explain scenario routes, which is useful for teams working on complex scenarios.\n\nNumerical aggregator\n\nA numerical aggregator lets you to apply functions like SUM or AVG to numerical values. Numerical aggregator then return the results in one bundle.\n\nOperation\n\nEvery time a module in a scenario performs an action, it counts as an operation. For example, when your scenario reads a record from Pipedrive, writes a row into a Google sheet, or posts a tweet, each counts as one operation.\n\nMore examples that count as operations:\n\nRead data from an app or webhook\n\nSearch for data in an app\n\nCreate data in an app\n\nUpdate data in an app\n\nDelete data from an app\n\nTransform data using the built-in tools\n\nAggregate a row of data into an array or text\n\nIterate a row of data\n\nDepending on the complexity of the process you’re automating, your scenario can perform anywhere from two operations to thousands of operations in a single run.\n\nNote\n\nThere is a limit on the number of operations according to your subscription.\n\nDon’t worry about using up all your operations before the end of the month or year. You can always buy extra operations or upgrade to a higher tier plan.\n\nSee Also Counting the number of operations.\n\nOperation phase\n\nOperation is the second phase of scenario execution. During the operation phase read and/or write operations are performed:\n\nThe read operation obtains the data needed by the modules in your scenario.\n\nThe write operation sends data to apps/services for further processing.\n\nRepeater\n\nWhen you need a module to perform a task multiple times, for example make an API call, use a repeater. Placing a repeater module before another module makes the subsequent module repeat its task. You can confirm by inspecting the bundles output by the subsequent module.\n\nSee Also Repeater section in Flow control article.\n\nResume error handling\n\nUse the Resume directive when you want scenario execution to continue even though an error occurs. The Resume directive allows subsequent modules continuing processing as if no error took place. The Scenario execution history displays the status as Success.\n\nRetry\n\nMake does not feature a retry error handling directive, though there are two workarounds that mimic its functionality.\n\nSee Also Retry workaround article.\n\nRollback error handling\n\nUse the Rollback directive when you want to mark the error and return modules to how they were before the scenario ran. The Rollback Directive stops the scenario execution immediately. Then a rollback phase starts on all modules to revert each module back to its initial state. The Rollback directive marks the scenario execution status as Error.\n\nNote\n\nThis is the default behavior if there is no error handler route and the Allow Storing Incomplete Executions setting under Scenario settings is not checked.\n\nSee Also Directives for error handling article.\n\nRollback phase\n\nRollback is a phase that occurs when there is an error during the operation or commit phase on any module. The scenario execution stops the operation or commit phase and starts the rollback phase, reversing all changes in data.\n\nNote\n\nSome modules do not support rollback and operations performed by these modules are irreversible.\n\nSee Also ACID modules.\n\nRouter\n\nA router allows you to add new routes to a scenario so you can branch your flow into several routes and process the data within each route differently.\n\nSee Also Router article.\n\nRun Once\n\nOnce a scenario is configured, you can execute it by clicking the play icon.\n\nThis way, you can verify that the scenario runs as you expect.\n\nIf everything is working properly, you can activate the scenario. Once activated, thescenario execute according to its schedule.\n\nIf everything does not run as expected, you can visit our error handling article to learn how to handle errors.\n\nScenario\n\nA scenario is a series of modules that users create to automate apps/services. Creating a scenario allows you to transfer and transform selected data between apps/services via modules.\n\nScenario execution\n\nWhenever your scenario runs, it constitutes one scenario execution. Make marks the scenario execution as either success, warning, or error. You can find this information on the right hand side of the Diagram or on the History tab.\n\nIn technical terms, scenario execution refers to a sequence of phases. Execution starts with the initialization phase, continues with at least one cycle composed of the operation and commit/rollback phases and ends with the finalization phase.\n\nIt is possible to receive emails when errors occur by enabling email notifications from the email notification options tab of the dashboard.\n\nScheduling\n\nMake allows you to define when and how often an active scenario runs. Use the Schedule setting panel under the Options tab and choose Scheduling to set your preferred schedule.\n\nSequential processing\n\nUsing the Sequential processing options allows you to monitor and resolve errors in greater detail. If you enable sequential processing, Make stops processing the task sequence until you resolve all incomplete executions. With sequential processing enabled, you can address all incomplete executions in the order in which they occurred.\n\nIf you disable Sequential processing, the scenario continues to run according to its schedule with repeated attempts to rerun the incomplete executions.\n\nSee Also Scenario settings article, Incomplete executions article.\n\nTable Aggregator\n\nYou can use a table aggregator to create a table from multiple bundles. The table aggregator merges values based on your specified column and row parameters and outputs into a single bundle. One possible use is compiling blog posts or emails into a single email summary.\n\nTeams\n\nUse teams to control and separate access to scenarios and other Make data. You can assign users to multiple teams and specific roles on each team. Members of a team have access only to scenarios and data that belong to their team and role.\n\nSee Also Teams article.\n\nTemplate\n\nA template is a pre-developed scenario that you can customize to your specific needs. Make has made many templates for you to quickly create useful scenarios.\n\nMake also allows you to submit your own templates for sharing with the Make community.\n\nText aggregator\n\nWhen a module requires text in a single bundle, use a text aggregator to merge values into a single bundle. You can map text aggregators the same way as modules or other tools to create the bundle you need.\n\nText Parser\n\nThe text parser tool allows you to add these modules:\n\nMatch pattern - allows you to find and extract text matching a search pattern. Match pattern uses regular expressions, a sequence of characters that specifies a search pattern. One example use is extracting email addresses from a document or the body of emails.\n\nReplace - searches for a specified value or regular expression, and replaces the result with the new value.\n\nGet elements from HTML - retrieves the desired elements from an HTML code.\n\nHTML to Text -allows you to convert HTML to plain text.\n\nGet elements from text - retrieves desired elements from text.\n\nTransaction processing\n\nMake uses transactional processing to describe the scenario execution cycle. A transaction consists of four phases during which Make creates or updates data in a way that ensures data integrity across apps and services. There are 4 phases:\n\nInitialization - creates all necessary connections and checks that all modules are ready.\n\nOperation - performs the reading and writing of data, retrieving and sending data from one service or module to another.\n\nCommit/rollback\n\nCommit - verifies all changes across modules and services and makes them permanent.\n\nRollback - when changes cannot be verified, the scenario ‘rolls back’ all changes, returning all data, modules, and services to their original states. The rollback phase protects data integrity in the event of an error.\n\nFinalization - closes all open connections (e.g. FTP connections, database connections, etc.) and completes the scenario.\n\nSee Also Scenarion execution, cycles, and phases.\n\nTrigger\n\nEvery scenario has a trigger, an event that starts your scenario. A scenario must have a trigger. There can only be one trigger for each scenario. When you create a new scenario, the first module you choose is your trigger for that scenario. Create a trigger by clicking on the empty module of a newly created scenario or moving the clock/lightning icon to another module.\n\nThere are two types of triggers:\n\nPolling -  routinely monitors a connected app/service \n\nInstant - also called webhooks that immediately execute the scenario \n\nWebhook\n\nWhen integrating with third-party apps/services, webhooks are a way for those apps to let Make know when something happens. A webhook is a notification containing data about an event, sent by one app to another app or site.\n\nMake uses webhooks as instant triggers to immediately execute the scenario. Webhooks create a URL that you can call from an external app or service, or from another Make scenario.\n\nPrev\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

$import_data,\n\n);\n\n// Sends import data to the webhook URL specified.\n\nwp_remote_post(\"https://hook.make.com/<webhook_id>\", $args);\n\n}\n\n add_action('pmxi_after_xml_import', Post\n\nCreates and publishes a new post or creates a new post as a draft.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Blogger's account.\n\n\n\n\nBlog\n\n\t\n\nSelect the blog where you want to create the post.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the post.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the post content.\n\n\n\n\nStatus\n\n\t\n\nSelect the status of the post:\n\nLive\n\nScheduled\n\nDraft\n\n\n\n\nDate Published\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date and time when this post was published.\n\n\n\n\nLabels\n\n\t\n\nEnter the labels when the post was published.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the post to geotag with a location.\n\n\n\n\nLatitude\n\n\t\n\nEnter the latitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nLongitude\n\n\t\n\nEnter the longitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nSpan\n\n\t\n\nEnter the span details for the location's viewport.\n\nDelete a Post\n\nPermanently removes a post (the deleted post cannot be restored anymore).\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Blogger's account.\n\n\n\n\nBlog\n\n\t\n\nSelect the blog where you want to create the post.\n\n\n\n\nPost ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Post ID you want to delete.\n\nPublish a Post\n\nPublishes a draft post.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Blogger's account.\n\n\n\n\nBlog\n\n\t\n\nSelect the blog where you want to create the post.\n\n\n\n\nPost ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Post ID you want to publish.\n\nRevert a Post\n\nReverts a published post to draft state.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Blogger's account.\n\n\n\n\nBlog\n\n\t\n\nSelect the blog where you want to create the post.\n\n\n\n\nPost ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Post ID you want to revert.\n\nUpdate a Post\n\nUpdates a published post.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Blogger's account.\n\n\n\n\nBlog\n\n\t\n\nSelect the blog where you want to create the post.\n\n\n\n\nPost ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Post ID you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the post.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the post content.\n\n\n\n\nStatus\n\n\t\n\nSelect the status of the post:\n\nLive\n\nScheduled\n\nDraft\n\n\n\n\nDate Published\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date and time when this post was published.\n\n\n\n\nLabels\n\n\t\n\nEnter the labels when the post was published.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the post to geotag with a location.\n\n\n\n\nLatitude\n\n\t\n\nEnter the latitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nLongitude\n\n\t\n\nEnter the longitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nSpan\n\n\t\n\nEnter the span details for the location's viewport.\n\nPossible problems\nUnable to update a post\n\nThe Update a post action does not allow to edit a draft (a post that's in progress). You can only update published posts.\n\nThe Watch posts trigger failed to download a post\n\nThe Blogger interface enables to download posts only assigned to one specific status. Blogger distinguishes three post statuses:\n\nPost in progress (draft status)\n\nPublished post (live status)\n\nScheduled post (scheduled status)\n\nIf you'd like to monitor posts in more statuses, you'll need to create a separate scenario for each status.\n\nBlogger\nGetting started with Blogger\nConnecting the Blogger to Make\nTriggers\nWatch Posts\nActions\nCreate a Post\nDelete a Post\nPublish a Post\nRevert a Post\nUpdate a Post\nPossible problems\nUnable to update a post\nThe Watch posts trigger failed to download a post\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
