Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityToggl\nToggl\n\nThe Toggl modules enable you to monitor, create, edit, delete, and retrieve clients, projects, reports, tasks, tags, users, workspaces, and time entries in your Toggl account.\n\nGetting Started with Toggl\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Toggl account - create an account at Toggl.\n\nConnecting Toggl to Make\n\nTo connect your Toggl account to Make you need to obtain an API Token from your Toggle account.\n\n1. Log in to your Toggl account.\n\n2. In the bottom-left corner, click your profile icon > Profile settings.\n\n3. In the API Token section, click and copy the token to your clipboard.\n\n4. Log in to your Make account and add a module from the Toggl app into an Make scenario.\n\n5. Click Add module next to the connection field.\n\n6. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n7. In the API Token field, enter the token copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nProjects\nWatch Projects\nCreate a Project\nUpdate a Project\nAdd a User to a Project\nGet a Project\nSearch Projects\nDelete a Project\nTime Entries\nWatch Time Entries\nGet a Running Time Entry\nCreate a Time Entry\nStop a Time Entry\nUpdate a Time Entry\nDelete a Time Entry\nReports\nGet a Summary Report\nGet a Detailed Report\nDownload a Detailed Report\nDownload a Summary Report\nExport Summary Report\nClients\nWatch Clients\nList Clients\nGet a Client\nCreate a Client\nUpdate a Client\nDelete a Client\nTasks\nWatch Tasks\nGet a Task\nCreate a Task\nUpdate a Task\nDelete a Task\nTags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nTriggers\nWatch Users\nWatch Workspaces\nWatch Tasks\nWatch Projects\nOther\nWatch Event\nGet an Object Name\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Workspace Projects\nCreate a Subscription\nValidate a Subscription\nToggl\nGetting Started with Toggl\nConnecting Toggl to Make\nProjects\nWatch Projects\nCreate a Project\nUpdate a Project\nAdd a User to a Project\nGet a Project\nSearch Projects\nDelete a Project\nTime Entries\nWatch Time Entries\nGet a Running Time Entry\nCreate a Time Entry\nStop a Time Entry\nUpdate a Time Entry\nDelete a Time Entry\nReports\nGet a Summary Report\nGet a Detailed Report\nDownload a Detailed Report\nDownload a Summary Report\nExport Summary Report\nClients\nWatch Clients\nList Clients\nGet a Client\nCreate a Client\nUpdate a Client\nDelete a Client\nTasks\nWatch Tasks\nGet a Task\nCreate a Task\nUpdate a Task\nDelete a Task\nTags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nTriggers\nWatch Users\nWatch Workspaces\nWatch Tasks\nWatch Projects\nOther\nWatch Event\nGet an Object Name\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Workspace Projects\nCreate a Subscription\nValidate a Subscription\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityTimeular\nTimeular\n\nThe Timeular modules allow you to monitor, create, update, show, start, stop, retrieve, list, and delete the current tracking, time entries, activities, tags, and mentions in your Timeular account.\n\nGetting Started with Timeular\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Timeular account - create an account at timeular.com/pricing/.\n\nConnecting Timeular to Make\n\nTo connect your Timeular account to Make you need to obtain the API Key, and API Secret from your Timeular account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your Timeular account.\n\n2. Click Settings and copy the API Key and API Secret values to a safe place.\n\n3. Log in to your Make account, add a module from the Timeular app into an Make scenario.\n\n4. Click Add next to the Connection field.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n6. In the API Key and API Secret fields, enter the API key and secret values copied in step 3 respectively.\n\n7. Click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nCurrent Tracking\nShow Current Tracking\n\nShows current tracking.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\nStart a Tracking\n\nStart a Tracking.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nStarted At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the time at which you want to start the tracking.\n\n\n\n\nNote\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the message text for tracking the time. You can tag or mention users at the end of the note text.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the keywords or tags for tracking.\n\n\n\n\nMentions\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the users you want to notify or mention in the tracking.\n\nUpdate a Tracking\n\nEdits the current tracking.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nActivity ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Activity ID whose tracking you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nStarted At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the time at which you want to start the tracking.\n\n\n\n\nNote\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the message text for tracking the time. You can tag or mention users at the end of the note text.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the keywords or tags for tracking.\n\n\n\n\nMentions\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the users you want to notify or mention in the tracking.\n\nStop a Tracking\n\nStops the current tracking.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nStopped at\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the time at which the tracking was stopped.\n\nTime Entries\nNote\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in Timeular once you add an instant trigger to your scenario.\n\nWatch Time Entries\n\nTriggers when a new time entry is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of time entries Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nSearch Time Entries\n\nReturns time entries in a given range.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nFrom Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a date to search the time entries from the specified date.\n\n\n\n\nTo Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a date to search the time entries until the specified date.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of time entries Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nCreate a Time Entry\n\nCreates a new time entry. The time entry will be created even if it overlaps with the other time entries - as a result existing time entries will be split or deleted in such a manner, that the new one will fit without overlapping.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nActivity ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Activity ID for which you want to create a time entry.\n\n\n\n\nStarted At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the start time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nStopped At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the stop time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nNote\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the note text for the time entry. You can tag or mention users at the end of the note text.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the keywords or tags for time entry.\n\n\n\n\nMentions\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the users you want to notify or mention about the time entry.\n\nDelete a Time Entry\n\nDelete a time entry.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nTime Entry ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Time Entry ID you want to delete.\n\nUpdate a Time Entry\n\nUpdates an existing time entry.\n\nBoth the new and old activity attached to the time entry has to belong to the same integration.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nActivity ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Activity ID for which you want to create a time entry.\n\n\n\n\nStarted At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the start time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nStopped At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the stop time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nNote\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the note text for the time entry. You can tag or mention users at the end of the note text.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the keywords or tags for time entry.\n\n\n\n\nMentions\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the users you want to notify or mention about the time entry.\n\nGet a Time Entry\n\nFinds a time entry by its ID.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nTime Entry ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Time Entry ID for whose details you want to retrieve.\n\nActivities\nList Activities\n\nLists all activities.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of activities Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nCreate an Activity\n\nCreates a new activity. It should have a name, a space, and a color.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nSpace ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Space ID in which you want to create the activity.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the name of the activity.\n\n\n\n\nColor\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the color you want to assign to the activity. For example, #34eb71 .\n\n\n\n\nIntegration\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the integration you want to apply for the activity.Note: You must have a Pro plan to use third-party integrations, zei is the default.\n\nUpdate an Activity\n\nUpdates the name and color of the activity.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nActivity ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Activity ID whose details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nNew Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a new name of the activity.\n\n\n\n\nNew Color\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the color you want to assign to the activity. For example, #34eb71 .\n\nArchive an Activity\n\nArchives an activity. It does not affect existing time entries and this activity will still be available in analytics.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nActivity ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Activity ID you want to archive.\n\nTags & Mentions\nCreate a Tag\n\nCreates a tag within the given space and scope (Timeular is the default).\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nSpace ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Space ID in which you want to create the tag.\n\n\n\n\nTag\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the tag name you want to create.\n\n\n\n\nScope\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the scope details in which you want to create.\n\n\n\n\nKey\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a key for the tag. For example, \"tagtag\".\n\nDelete a Tag\n\nDeletes the given tag.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nTag ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Tag ID you want to delete.\n\nUpdate a Tag\n\nCreates a new label for the tag.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nTag ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Tag ID whose details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nNew Label\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a new tag name. The hashtag symbol # is added automatically.\n\nCreate a Mention\n\nCreates a mention within the given space and scope (Timeular is the default).\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nSpace ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Space ID in which you want to create the mention.\n\n\n\n\nMention\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the mention name.\n\n\n\n\nScope\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the scope details in which you want to create the mention.\n\n\n\n\nKey\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a key for the mention. For example, mention.\n\nUpdate a Mention\n\nCreates a new mention label.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nMention ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Mention ID whose details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nLabel\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a new mention name. The Hashtag symbol @ added automatically.\n\nDelete a Mention\n\nDeletes the given mention.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nMention ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Mention ID whose details you want to delete.\n\nList Tags\n\nLists all tags.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of tags Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nList Mention\n\nLists all mentions.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of mentions Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nOther\nNote\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in Timeular once you add an instant trigger to your scenario.\n\nWatch for Tracking Events\n\nTriggers when an event given in its type parameter occurs.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a webhook name.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nEvent\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the tracking events you want to watch.\n\nWatch for Time Entry Events\n\nTriggers when an event given in its type parameter occurs.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a webhook name.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nEvent\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the events whose time entry events you want to watch.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Timeular account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.timeular.com/apiFor example: v1/activities\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Timeular API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST to create a new entry.\n\nPUT to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH to make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE to delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Webhook Events\n\nThe following API call returns all the webhook events from your Timeular account:\n\nURL:/v1/webhooks/event\n\nMethod:GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > events. In our example, 7 webhook events were returned:\n\nTimeular\nGetting Started with Timeular\nConnecting Timeular to Make\nCurrent Tracking\nShow Current Tracking\nStart a Tracking\nUpdate a Tracking\nStop a Tracking\nTime Entries\nWatch Time Entries\nSearch Time Entries\nCreate a Time Entry\nDelete a Time Entry\nUpdate a Time Entry\nGet a Time Entry\nActivities\nList Activities\nCreate an Activity\nUpdate an Activity\nArchive an Activity\nTags & Mentions\nCreate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nCreate a Mention\nUpdate a Mention\nDelete a Mention\nList Tags\nList Mention\nOther\nWatch for Tracking Events\nWatch for Time Entry Events\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Webhook Events\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityTMetric\nTMetric\n\nThe TMetric modules allow you to watch, create, update, list, and delete the tasks, and time entries in your TMetrict account.\n\nGetting Started with TMetric\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA TMetric account\n\nIn order to use TMetric with Make, it is necessary to have a TMetric account. If you do not have one, you can create a TMetric account at id.tmetric.com/core/register.\n\nConnecting TMetric to Make\n\nTo connect your TMetric account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your TMetric account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your TMetric account and open your Dashboard.\n\n2. Click Your Profile Name in the bottom-left corner > My Profile.\n\n3. Click Get New API Token and copy the token to your clipboard.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the TMetric module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n6. In the API Token field, enter the token copied in step 3 and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTasks\nWatch New Tasks\n\nTriggers when a new task is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nEnter the maximum number of tasks Make should return during one scenario execution cycle.\n\n\n\n\nAssignee List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the assignees whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nGroup List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the groups whose associated tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nProject List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the projects whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nTag List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the keywords to filter the tasks when searching.\n\n\n\n\nCompleted\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to watch the completed tasks:\n\nYes\n\nNo\n\nNot defined\n\nCreate a Task\n\nCreates a task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID for which you want to create the task.\n\n\n\n\nAssignee ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Assignee ID to whom you want to assign the task.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter the details of the task.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Project ID to which the task belongs to.\n\n\n\n\nTag Identifiers\n\n\t\n\nAdd the tag or keywords to filter the task when searching.\n\n\n\n\nIs Completed\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if the task is completed.\n\n\n\n\nBudget Size\n\n\t\n\nEnter the budget details allocated for the task.\n\n\n\n\nCreator ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the user who created this task.\n\n\n\n\nExternal Issue ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the External Issue ID of the task.\n\n\n\n\nIntegration ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Integration ID if the task is tracked by integrating with another app.\n\n\n\n\nIntegration URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Integration URL for the task.\n\n\n\n\nRelative Issue URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the issue URL for which this task is being created.\n\n\n\n\nProject Task ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Project Task ID associated with the task.\n\n\n\n\nShow Issue ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to show the Issue ID in the task.\n\nDelete a Task\n\nDeletes a task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID whose task you want to delete.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Task ID you want to delete.\n\nGet a Task\n\nGets a single task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID whose task details you want to retrieve.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Task ID whose details you want to retrieve.\n\nList Tasks\n\nLists all tasks for an account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nAssignee IDs List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the assignees whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nGroup IDs List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the groups whose associated tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nProject IDs List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the projects whose tasks you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nTag IDs List\n\n\t\n\nAdd the keywords to filter the tasks when searching.\n\n\n\n\nCompleted\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to watch the completed tasks:\n\nYes\n\nNo\n\nNot defined\n\nTime Entries\nCreate a Time Entry\n\nCreates a time entry.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID for which you want to create the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nUser Profile ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the User Profile ID whose time entry you are creating.\n\n\n\n\nStart Time\n\n\t\n\nEnter the start time.\n\n\n\n\nEnd Time\n\n\t\n\nEnter the end time.\n\n\n\n\nTime Duration\n\n\t\n\nEnter the duration of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nProject Name\n\n\t\n\nSelect the project name associated with the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nTags Identifiers\n\n\t\n\nAdd the keywords to filter the time entries when searching.\n\n\n\n\nIs Billable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if this time entry is billable.\n\n\n\n\nIs Invoiced\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if the time entry is invoiced.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter the details for creating the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Project ID associated with the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nProject Task ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Project Task ID associated with the time entry.\n\nList Time Entries\n\nLists all-time entries.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID whose time entries you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nUser Profile ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the User Profile ID whose time entries you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nUse UTC Time\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to list the time entries in UTC Time:\n\nYes\n\nNo\n\nNot defined\n\n\n\n\nVersion\n\n\t\n\nEnter the version of the time entries you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nLatest Version\n\n\t\n\nEnter the latest version of the time entries you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nInclude Deleted\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to list the deleted time entries:\n\nYes\n\nNo\n\nNot defined\n\n\n\n\nTruncate\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to list the ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Time Entry ID you want to update or delete.\n\n\n\n\nStart Time\n\n\t\n\nEnter the start time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nEnd Time\n\n\t\n\nEnter the end time of the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nTime Duration\n\n\t\n\nEnter the duration of the time entry\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter the details for updating or deleting the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Project ID associated with the time entry.\n\n\n\n\nIs Billable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if this time entry is billable.\n\n\n\n\nIs Invoiced\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if the time entry is invoiced.\n\n\n\n\nTags Identifiers\n\n\t\n\nAdd the keywords to filter the time entries when searching.\n\n\n\n\nIs Deleted\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if the time entry is deleted.\n\nTimer\nUpdate a Timer\n\nUpdates, starts, and stops a timer.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your TMetric connection.\n\n\n\n\nAccount ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Account ID for which you want to update with Todoist\n\nThe Todoist modules allow you to monitor, create, update, list, and delete projects, labels, tasks, comments, and more in your Todoist account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Todoist account\n\nIn order to use Todoist with Make, it is necessary to have a Todoist account. If you do not have one, you can create a Todoist account at todoist.com.\n\nConnecting Todoist to Make\n\nTo connect Todoist to Make you must connect your Todoist account to Make. To do so, follow the general instructions for Connecting to services.\n\nAfter you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Todoist website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Agree button.\n\nEvents\nNew Event\nProjects\nList Projects\nGet a Project\nCreate a Project\nUpdate a Project\nDelete a Project\nLabels\nList Labels\n\nRetrieves labels from your Todoist account.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of labels Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet a Label\n\nRetrieves information about a label.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nLabel ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Label ID of the label you want to retrieve information about.\n\nCreate a Label\n\nCreates a label.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read_write\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the new label.\n\nUpdate a Label\n\nChanges the name of the label.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read_write\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nLabel ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the label ID of the label you want to edit.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter a new name for the label.\n\nDelete a Label\n\nDeletes a label.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:delete\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nLabel ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Label ID of the label you want to delete.\n\nTasks\nList Uncompleted Tasks\n\nLists all uncompleted tasks.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nQuery\n\n\t\n\nEnter a keyword or phrase to list the tasks that match the specified tasks.\n\n\n\n\nProject\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the project whose incomplete tasks you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of tasks Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet a Task\n\nRetrieves details about a specified task.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Task ID of the task you want to retrieve information about.\n\nCreate a Task\n\nCreates a new task.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read_write\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the task content.\n\n\n\n\nProject\n\n\t\n\nSelect the project or map the task ID. If not set, the task is put into the user’s Inbox.\n\n\n\n\nLabels\n\n\t\n\nSelect the labels you want to associate with the task.\n\n\n\n\nDue date\n\n\t\n\nDate\n\nEnter the date in YYYY-MM-DD format or YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SS.\n\nHuman-readable representation of due date\n\nWhat you type:\n\n\t\n\nWhat Todoist understands:\n\n\n\n\ntoday\n\n\t\n\nToday (tod also works)\n\n\n\n\ntomorrow\n\n\t\n\nTomorrow (tom also works)\n\n\n\n\nnext week\n\n\t\n\nThe next Monday by default (this can be changed in your Settings)\n\n\n\n\nnext month\n\n\t\n\n1st day of the next month\n\n\n\n\njan 27\n\n\t\n\nJan 27 (27 jan, 27/1 also works)\n\n\n\n\n01/27/2016\n\n\t\n\nJanuary 27, 2016 (27/01/2016, 2016/01/27, 2016-01-27 also work)\n\n\n\n\n27th\n\n\t\n\n27th day of the current month\n\n\n\n\nmid January\n\n\t\n\nJanuary 15th\n\n\n\n\nend of month\n\n\t\n\nLast day of the current month\n\n\n\n\ntoday at 10\n\n\t\n\nToday at 10am\n\n\n\n\ntomorrow at 16:00\n\n\t\n\nTomorrow at 4pm\n\n\n\n\nFri @ 7pm\n\n\t\n\nFriday at 7pm (Friday @ 7pm, Fri at 7pm, Fri at 19:00 also work)\n\n\n\n\n6pm\n\n\t\n\nToday at 6pm (unless 6pm has passed, in which case tomorrow)\n\n\n\n\nin 5 days\n\n\t\n\n5 days from today (+5 days also works)\n\n\n\n\nin 3 weeks\n\n\t\n\n3 weeks from today\n\n\n\n\nin 2 hours\n\n\t\n\n2 hours from now\n\nIs recurring\n\nSelect whether the task should be set as recurring.\n\n\n\n\nPriority\n\n\t\n\nSelect the task priority.\n\n\n\n\nParent ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the ID of the parent task. Leave the field empty for root tasks.\n\n\n\n\nResponsible\n\n\t\n\nSelect the user who is responsible for accomplishing the current task.\n\nThis works for shared projects only.\n\n\n\n\nAssigned by\n\n\t\n\nSelect the user who has assigned this task.\n\nThis works for shared projects only.\n\n\n\n\nAuto reminder\n\n\t\n\nWhen this option is enabled, the default reminder will be added to the task if it has a due date with a time set.\n\nUpdate a Task\n\nEdits a specified task.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read_write\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Task ID of the task you want to update.\n\nPlease find the descriptions of the fields in the Create a Task section above.\n\nDelete a Task\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Task ID of the task you want to delete.\n\nComplete a Task\n\nCompletes a task and all its descendants.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Todoist account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Task ID of the task you want to set as complete.\n\n\n\n\nDate completed\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date of completion of the task (in UTC). If left empty, the server will set the value to the current time. The list of supported date and time formats.\n\nUncomplete a Task\n\nUncompletes an unarchived task and all its ancestors.\n\nRequired Permissions: data:read_write\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a For example, if your URL is https://make.teamwork.com, the domain is make.\n\nOptional: Switch on the Show advanced settings toggle and enter your custom app client credentials. For more information, refer to Teamwork documentation.\n\nIf requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/teamwork2.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityStackby\nStackby\n\nThe Stackby modules allow you to watch, create, update, and search the rows in your Stackby account.\n\nGetting Started with Stackby\nPrerequisites:\n\nA Stackby account\n\nIn order to use Stackby with Make, it is necessary to have a Stackby account. If you do not have one, you can create a Stackby account at stackby.com/signup.\n\nConnecting Stackby to Make\n\nTo connect your Stackby account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your Stackby account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Login to your Stackby account.\n\n2. Click your Profile Icon > Account > Create API Key.\n\n3. Copy the API Key to your clipboard.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the Stackby module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection\n\n6. In the API Key field, enter the API key copied in step 3 and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\nWatch Records\n\nReturns all newly created rows in a view.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Stackby account.\n\n\n\n\nWorkspace\n\n\t\n\nSelect the workspace whose stack records you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nStack\n\n\t\n\nSelect the stack whose records you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table whose records you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nView\n\n\t\n\nSelect the type of records you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of records Make should return during one scenario execution cycle.\n\nActions\nCreate a Row\n\nCreates a new row in any table in Stackby.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Stackby account.\n\n\n\n\nWorkspace\n\n\t\n\nSelect the workspace whose table you want to add a row.\n\n\n\n\nStack\n\n\t\n\nSelect the stack whose table you want to add a row.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table where you want to add a row. For example, Contacts. When you select a table type, the field auto-populates the fields which you need to fill for adding the row.\n\nUpdate a Row\n\nUpdates a row by its ID.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Stackby account.\n\n\n\n\nWorkspace\n\n\t\n\nSelect the workspace whose table's row details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nStack\n\n\t\n\nSelect the stack whose table's row details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table whose row details you want to update. For example, Contacts. When you select a table type, the field auto-populates the fields which you need to update.\n\n\n\n\nRow ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Row ID whose details you want to update.\n\nSearches\nSearch Rows\n\nSearches for any specific row or returns all rows.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Stackby account.\n\n\n\n\nWorkspace\n\n\t\n\nSelect the workspace whose table's rows you want to search.\n\n\n\n\nStack\n\n\t\n\nSelect the stack whose table's rows you want to search.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table whose rows you want to search for.\n\n\n\n\nSearch Formula\n\n\t\n\nEnter the formula to search the specific rows. For example, columnName = sample.\n\n\n\n\nSort\n\n\t\n\nAdd the options to sort the rows:\n\nField\n\nSelect the field to sort. For example, Phone.\n\nDirection\n\nSelect the order in which you want to list the rows:\n\nAscending\n\nDescending\n\n\n\n\nView\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table type whose rows you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nMax Record\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of rows Make should return during one scenario execution cycle.\n\nStackby\nGetting Started with Stackby\nPrerequisites:\nConnecting Stackby to Make\nTriggers\nWatch Records\nActions\nCreate a Row\nUpdate a Row\nSearches\nSearch Rows\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

SimplyBook.me modules in Make, you can:\n\nwatch, create, update, search, and cancel bookings, create a booking's comment, and retrieve booking details and links\n\ncreate, update, retrieve, search, and delete clients\n\ncreate, update, retrieve, search, and delete notes\n\nsearch and retrieve available slots\n\ncreate and retrieve reports\n\nsearch and retrieve invoices\n\napply a promo code\n\nissue a gift card\n\naccept a payment\n\nTo get started with SimplyBook.me, create an account at simplybook.me\n\nConnect SimplyBook.me to Make\n\nTo connect SimplyBook.me app:\n\nLog in to your SimplyBook.me account.\n\nLog in to your Make account, insert a SimplyBook.me module in your scenario, and click the Add button next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Company fields, enter your company name.\n\nIn the Login and Password fields, enter your account credentials and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit scenario and add more Simplybook.me modules. webhooks:\n\nOpen any watch Booking Events modules, click Add, enter a name for the webhook, click Save and copy the URL to your clipboard.\n\nLog in to your SimplyBook.me account, click Custom Features, and enable the API.\n\nEnable the required triggers, in the Callback URL field, enter the URL address copied in step 1, and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully set up the webhooks and will modules in Make, you can watch, list, get, append, update, link and delete your rows.\n\nTo get started with SeaTable, create an account at seatable.io.\n\nRefer to the SeaTable API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect SeaTable to Make\n\nTo connect your SeaTable account to Make, you must first obtain the API Key from your SeaTable account.\n\nTo establish the connection:\n\nLog in to your SeaTable account.\n\nIn the left sidebar, go to Bases, then click Add a base or folder.\n\nUse the dropdown menu to choose the way you want to create your base.\n\nOptional: Enter a name and choose a color for the base.\n\nClick the three dots near the base name > Advanced > API Token.\n\nEnter a name for your App, choose Read-Write as Permission and click Submit.\n\nCopy the Access token value shown and store it in a safe place. You will use this key in the API Key field in Make.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a SeaTable module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied in Step 7.\n\nNote: In the Server field, the public SAAS Server is https://cloud.seatable.io. To use your own on-premise SeaTable you have to add something else.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more SeaTable modules. RegFox.\n\nCopy the new API key.\n\nGo to your Make scenario and select the RegFox module you want to use.\n\nUnder Connection, click Add, then give your new connection a name.\n\nPaste the API key in the field provided, then click Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now begin editing your scenario and adding more RegFox modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nSetting up RegFox webhooks\n\nThis app makes use of webhooks to instantly trigger a scenario when an event occurs. Follow the steps below to set them up.\n\nGo to your Make scenario and select the RegFox Watch module you want to use.\n\nUnder Webhook, click Add, then give your new webhook a name.\n\nAdd or select the connection you want to use.\n\nEnter your account ID. You can find this ID number in your RegFox account URL.\n\nSelect which type of event you want to monitor.\n\nClick Save.\n\nMake attaches the webhook automatically for you in your RegFox account. The scenario will now trigger when an event occurs.\n\nRegFox\nConnect RegFox to Make\nSetting up RegFox webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

cycle.\n\nActions\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your RapidReg account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://rapidreg.com/api. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of use - Account information\n\nThe following API call returns your account information.\n\nURL: v1/get/account\n\nMethod: GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > account.\n\nSetting up <app> webhooks\n\n(if needed)\n\nRapidReg\nConnecting RapidReg to Make\nTriggers\nWatch New Registrations\nActions\nMake an API Call\nExample of use - Account information\nSetting up <app> webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

PomoDoneApp modules, you can:\n\nWatch the completed tasks, and task timers\n\nCreate a task\n\nCall APIs\n\nTo get started with the PomoDoneApp, create an account at pomodoneapp.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in theMake scenario, and not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnect PomoDoneApp with Make\n\nTo connect the PomoDoneApp app with the Make:\n\nLog in to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\nClick My Settings > Your API key and copy the API key to a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make and add a module from the PomoDoneApp into a Make scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Connection field.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the details copied in step 2, and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully connected the PomoDoneApp app with Make and can now build scenarios.\n\nTasks\n\nYou can create the tasks, watch the completed tasks, and timers for the tasks using the following modules.\n\nNote\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in PomoDone once you add an instant trigger to your Make.\n\nWatch Task Done\n\nTriggers when a task has been marked as done.\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\nWatch Timer Start\n\nTriggers when a app timer has been started.\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\nWatch Timer Stop\n\nTriggers when a app timer has been stopped.\n\nWebhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\nCreate a Task\n\nCreates a task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a name for the task.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a task details.\n\n\n\n\nProject\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map a project for which you want to create a task.\n\n\n\n\nDue Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) a date by when you want the task to completed. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\nOther\n\nYou can call APIs using the following module.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PomoDoneApp account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.pomodoneapp.com. For example: /import/projects/.\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the PomoDoneApp API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of use - Get Projects\n\nThe following API call lists the projects from your PomoDoneApp account:\n\nURL:\n\n/import/projects/\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundles > Body.\n\nIn our example, 7 projects were returned:\n\nPomoDoneApp\nConnect PomoDoneApp with Make\nTasks\nWatch Task Done\nWatch Timer Start\nWatch Timer Stop\nCreate a Task\nOther\nMake an API Call\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Therefore both types of clients are supported now.\n\nParameter Assignee - added a selection for \"role\". Therefore it is easier to work with assignees, because they are now retrieved by a role.\n\nCustom fields - all create/update modules that work with custom fields now dynamically generate a ready-to-use block of fields.\n\nItems in Create an Invoice/Proposal - modules now support block of \"items\".\n\nItems in Update an Invoice/Proposal - modules now support adding/removing blocks with \"items\".\n\nParameter Status - dynamically retrieved from the account for every entity that works with status.\n\nPlutio\nConnecting Plutio to Make\nProjects\nWatch Projects\nSearch Projects\nGet a Project\nCreate a Project\nUpdate a Project\nDelete a Project\nProposals\nWatch Proposals\nSearch Proposals\nGet a Proposal\nCreate a Proposal\nUpdate a Proposal\nDelete a Proposal\nInvoices\nWatch Invoices\nSearch Invoices\nGet an Invoice\nCreate an Invoice\nUpdate an Invoice\nDelete an Invoice\nTask Boards\nWatch Task Boards\nSearch Task Board\nGet a Task Board\nCreate a Task Board\nUpdate a Task Board\nCopy a Task Board\nDelete a Task Board\nTask Groups\nWatch Task Groups\nSearch Task Groups\nGet a Task Groups\nCreate a Task Group\nUpdate a Task Group\nCopy a Task Group\nDelete a Task Group\nBlocks\nSearch Blocks\nGet a Block\nCreate a Block\nDelete a Block\nTasks\nWatch Tasks\nSearch Tasks\nGet a Task\nCreate a Task\nUpdate a Task\nCopy a Task\nMove a Task\nDelete a Task\nPeople\nWatch People\nSearch People\nGet a Person\nCreate a Person\nUpdate a Person\nDelete a Person\nPlutio Polling Triggers\nWatch Forms\nWatch Templates\nOther\nWatch Notifications\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Companies\nChange log between Plutio [v2] and Plutio [v1]\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Tracker\n\nThe Pivotal Tracker modules allow you to monitor, create, update, list, retrieve, and delete the projects, and stories in your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\nGetting Started with Pivotal Tracker\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Pivotal Tracker account\n\nIn order to use Pivotal Tracker with Make, it is necessary to have a Pivotal Tracker account. If you do not have one, you can create a Pivotal Tracker account at pivotaltracker.com.\n\nConnecting Pivotal Tracker to Make\n\nTo connect your Pivotal Tracker account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your Pivotal Tracker account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n2. Click Your Account Name > Profile.\n\n3. Navigate to the API Token section and copy the token to your clipboard.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the Pivotal Tracker module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for your connection.\n\n6. In the Pivotal Tracker API Token field, enter token copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nProject\nStory\nWatch Stories\n\nTriggers when a new story is added to a project.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID whose stories you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of stories Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Properties\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the property details you want to retrieve.\n\nList Stories\n\nRetrieves a list of the stories of a project.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of projects Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID whose stories you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Properties\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the property details you want to retrieve.\n\nCreate a Story\n\nCreate a new story in a project.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID for which you are creating the story.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the project name.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the details of the project.\n\n\n\n\nEstimate\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the number of points for the story.\n\n\n\n\nStory Type\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the story type. For example, Feature.\n\n\n\n\nLabels\n\n\t\n\nAdd the labels for the story. For example, new.\n\n\n\n\nRequested By\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the user who requested this story. For example, customer name.\n\n\n\n\nLinked Project Integration\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the link of this story to other tools, such as Jira. For more information, see the Pivotal Tracker documentation about using project integrations.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Properties\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the properties you want to retrieve for the project.\n\nGet a Story\n\nGets the information of a story.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID for which you are creating the story.\n\n\n\n\nStory ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Story ID whose details you want to retrieve.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Properties\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the properties you want to retrieve in the story details.\n\nUpdate a Story\n\nUpdates the parameters of a story.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID for which you are creating the story.\n\n\n\n\nStory ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Story ID whose details you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the new Project ID with which you want to associate the story.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the new name for the story.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the details of the project.\n\n\n\n\nStory Type\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the story type. For example, Feature.\n\n\n\n\nState\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the status of the story. For example, Accepted.\n\n\n\n\nEstimate\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the number of points for the story.\n\n\n\n\nLabels\n\n\t\n\nAdd the labels for the story. For example, new.\n\n\n\n\nRequested By\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the user who requested this story. For example, customer name.\n\n\n\n\nIntegration\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the linked integration of this story to other tools, such as Jira. For more information, see the Pivotal Tracker documentation about using project integrations.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Properties\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the properties you want to retrieve for the project.\n\nDelete a Story\n\nDeletes a story.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pivotal Tracker account.\n\n\n\n\nProject ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Project ID whose story you want to delete\n\n\n\n\nStory ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Story ID you want to delete.\n\nOther\nPivotal Tracker\nGetting Started with Pivotal Tracker\nConnecting Pivotal Tracker to Make\nProject\nWatch Project\nList Projects\nCreate a Project\nGet a Project\nUpdate a Project\nDelete a Project\nStory\nWatch Stories\nList Stories\nCreate a Story\nGet a Story\nUpdate a Story\nDelete a Story\nOther\nWatch Activities\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Stories\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

If you do not have one, you can create a ReferralHero account at referralhero.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting ReferralHero to Make\n\nTo connect your ReferralHero account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your ReferralHero account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your ReferralHero account and open your Dashboard.\n\nClick Account > API.\n\nCopy the API token to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the ReferralHero module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Token field, enter the token details copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nSubscribers\n\nSee the Setting Up the ReferralHero Webhooks to add the webhook in your ReferralHero account.\n\nWatch New Subscribers added to your campaign.\nWatch Deleted Subscribers\nList Subscribers\nGet a Subscriber\nCreate a Subscriber\nUpdate a Subscriber\nDelete a Subscriber\nReferrals\nConfirm a Referral\nLists\nList Lists\nCreate a List\nRewards\n\nSee the Setting Up the ReferralHero Webhooks to add the webhook in your ReferralHero account.\n\nWatch Unlocked Rewards\nList Rewards\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Subscribers\nSetting Up the ReferralHero Webhooks\n\nOpen any Watch module, establish a connection as mentioned in the respective modules, click Save and copy the URL address to your clipboard. Click OK and save the trigger.\n\nLog in to your ReferralHero account.\n\nSelect the campaign for which you want to add the webhooks.\n\nClick Installation Instructions > Integrations > Webhooks > +New Webhook.\n\nAdd the URL address copied in step 1 and select the events for which you want to receive the triggers. When you add the URL address in the URL field, remove the prefix https:// as the copied URL already has that part.\n\nClick Create Webhook.\n\nYou have successfully added the webhook.\n\nGo to Make and run the webhook scenario to receive the triggers for the selected events.\n\nReferralHero\nGetting Started with ReferralHero\nConnecting ReferralHero to Make\nSubscribers\nWatch New Subscribers added to your campaign.\nWatch Deleted Subscribers\nList Subscribers\nGet a Subscriber\nCreate a Subscriber\nUpdate a Subscriber\nDelete a Subscriber\nReferrals\nConfirm a Referral\nLists\nList Lists\nCreate a List\nRewards\nWatch Unlocked Rewards\nList Rewards\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Subscribers\nSetting Up the ReferralHero Webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

allow you to watch, create, update, retrieve, comments, contacts, items, organizations, files, applications, status, and tasks in your Podio account.\n\nGetting Started with Podio\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Podio account\n\nIn order to use Podio with Make, it is necessary to have a Podio account. If you do not have one, you can create a Podio account at podio.com/signup.\n\nConnecting Podio to Make\n\n1. Go to Make and open the Podio module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n2. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection and click Continue.\n\n3. Confirm the access by clicking the Grant Access.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\nWatch Apps\n\nTriggers when a new application is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a For subscription information, refer to the Salesforce Pardot Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the Salesforce Pardot API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Salesforce Pardot to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your Business Unit ID in Salesforce Pardot.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your Pardot Business Unit ID in Salesforce Pardot\n\nTo obtain your Pardot Business Unit ID from your Salesforce Pardot account:\n\nLog in to your Salesforce Pardot account.\n\nIn the upper right corner, click the Setup  icon.\n\nClick Marketing Setup.\n\nClick Business Unit Setup and then click + Add New Business Unit.\n\nIn the Business Unit Name field, enter Make.\n\nIn the Setup Admin field, select the user who will administrate this Business Unit.\n\nClick Save.\n\nCopy the Business Unit ID value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the Pardot Business Unit ID field in Make.\n\nNote: You can use the Business Unit ID only when the Business Unit has the Enabled status.\n\nEstablish the connection with Salesforce Pardot in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Salesforce Pardot module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Pardot Business Unit ID field, enter the Pardot Business Unit ID copied above.\n\nIn the Account Type field, select the account type that you want to connect Make to.\n\nOptional: Switch on the Show advanced settings toggle and enter your custom app client credentials. For more information, refer to Salesforce app documentation,\n\nNote: when creating a custom app, use the following data:\n\nCallback URL: https://www.make.com/oauth/cb/salesforce-pardot\n\nSelected OAuth Scopes:\n\nManage Pardot services (pardot_api)\n\nPerform requests at any time (refresh_token, offline_access)\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Salesforce Pardot modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Salesforce Pardot Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nRecords\n\nWith the help of these modules, you can manage records in your Salesforce Pardot account.\n\nWatch Records\nSearch Records\nCreate a Record\nGet a Record\nUpdate a Record\nDelete a Record\nFiles and folders\n\nWith the help of these modules, you can manage files and folders in your Salesforce Pardot account.\n\nSearch Files\nSearch Folders\nSearch Folder Content\nUpload a File\nGet a File\nGet a Folder\nGet a Folder Content\nDelete a File\nOther\nMake an API Call\nSalesforce Pardot\nConnect Salesforce Pardot to Make\nObtain your Pardot Business Unit ID in Salesforce Pardot\nEstablish the connection with Salesforce Pardot in Make\nBuild Salesforce Pardot Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

modules in Make, you can:\n\nsearch, retrieve, create, update, and delete contacts\n\nsearch, retrieve, create, and update tasks\n\nwatch, search, retrieve, create, update, and delete actions\n\nsearch, retrieve, create, and update records\n\nadd, retrieve, download, and delete a file, and list file history\n\nTo get started with Planfix, create an account at scenario.\n\nLog in to your Planfix account.\n\nClick Settings > Account Management.\n\nClick XML API and copy the API Key and Authorization token values to a safe place.\n\nLog in to successfully established the connection. Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityPipefy\nPipefy\n\nWith Pipefy modules in Make, you can manage the triggers, pipes, and tables in your Pipefy account.\n\nTo use the Pipefy modules, you must have a Pipefy account. You can create an account at pipefy.com/signup/.\n\nRefer to the Pipefy API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Pipefy to Make\n\nTo connect your Pipefy account to Make, you must first obtain the API Key from your Pipefy account.\n\nTo establish the connection:\n\nLog in to your Pipefy account.\n\nClick Your Profile Icon > Account Preferences > Personal Access Tokens > Generate a new token.\n\nEnter a name for the token and click Save.\n\nCopy the API token to your clipboard and click Save.\n\nLog in to your Make, add a Pipefy module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied in Step 4.\n\nOptional: In the Subdomain field, enter your account domain details. For example, if your full domain is bestsaas.pipefy.com then your subdomain is bestsaas.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Pipefy modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Pipefy Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTriggers\n\nWatch New Cards\n\nWatch Moved Cards\n\nWatch Done Cards\n\nWatch Overdue Cards\n\nWatch Late Cards\n\nWatch Expired Cards\n\nWatch Card Field Update\n\nNote\n\nWebhooks may take a few minutes to trigger due to delays caused by Pipefy servers.\n\nCreate a Card\n\nCreate a Card v1 has been deprecated. To use the latest Pipefy features, switch to the new Create a Card module at your earliest convenience.\n\nList Cards\n\nGet a Phase\n\nGet a Card Info\n\nUpdate a Card\n\nUpdate a Card Field\n\nMove a Card to Phase\n\nDelete a Card\n\nTables\n\nCreate a Table\n\nCreate a Table Record\n\nList Table Records\n\nGet a Table Record\n\nUpdate a Table Record\n\nDelete a Table Record\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nExecute a GraphQL Query\n\nPipefy\nConnect Pipefy to Make\nBuild Pipefy Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityPinboard\nPinboard\n\nWith the Pinboard modules, you can create and watch the bookmark in your Pinboard account.\n\nTo get started with the Pinboard, create an account at pinboard.com\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnect Pinboard with Make\n\nTo connect the Pinboard app with the Make:\n\nLog in to your Pinboard account.\n\nClick Settings > Password and copy the API Key to a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make account and add a module from the Pinboard into a Make scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Connection field.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field enter the details copied in step 2 and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully connected the Pinboard app with Make and can now build scenarios.\n\nBookmarks\n\nYou can watch the bookmarks using the following module.\n\nWatch Bookmarks\n\nWatches for new bookmarks.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pinboard account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of bookmarks Make will return during one execution cycle. The default value is 2.\n\nCreate a Bookmark\n\nCreates a new bookmark.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pinboard account.\n\n\n\n\nBookmark URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the URL address of the item for which you want to create the bookmark.\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the bookmark name.\n\n\n\n\nExtended\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the bookmark details.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the tags. You can list up to 100 tags.\n\n\n\n\nDatetime\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) creation time for this bookmark. By default, it is the current time. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\nNote\n\nDatestamps more than 10 minutes ahead of server time reset to the current server time.\n\n\n\n\nReplace\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to replace any existing bookmark with this URL. The default is Yes. If set to No, returns an error if the bookmark exists.\n\n\n\n\nShared\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether make the bookmark public. The default is Yes unless you enable the setting, save all bookmarks as private, then the default value is No.\n\n\n\n\nTo Read\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to mark the bookmark as unread. The default is No.\n\nOthers\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pinboard account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.pinboard.in .For example, /v1/posts/all.\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Pinboard API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - Returns all bookmarks\n\nThe following API call returns all bookmarks in your Pinboard account:\n\nURL:\n\n/v1/posts/all\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundles > Body > posts > post.\n\nIn our example, 12 bookmarks were returned:\n\nPinboard\nConnect Pinboard with Make\nBookmarks\nWatch Bookmarks\nCreate a Bookmark\nOthers\nMake an API Call\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityNeaktor\nNeaktor\n\nWith Neaktor modules in Make, you can create, update, monitor, and delete your tasks in your Neaktor account and make API calls.\n\nTo get started with Neaktor, create an account at app.neaktor.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory.\n\nConnect Neaktor to Make\n\nTo make a connection to Neaktor you need to obtain a Client ID and Client Secret from your Neaktor account.\n\nLog in to your Neaktor account.\n\nClick the 3-line menu icon at the top of the page, then click Integrations.\n\nClick API keys.\n\nClick Generate new key.\n\nFrom the two options, select OAuth2 keychain. Click Create API key.\n\nChange the API key status to Read and write.\n\nCopy the both the Client ID and Secret Key to your clipboard.\n\nGo to your Make scenario and select the Neaktor module you want to use.\n\nUnder Connection, click Add.\n\nGive your new connection a name.\n\nPaste the Client ID and Client secret in the fields below.\n\nClick Save.\n\nA prompt appears asking to grant Make read and write access to your Neaktor account data. Click allow.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection.\n\nTasks\nWatch Tasks\nSearch Tasks\nGet a Task\nCreate a Task\nUpdate a Task\nDelete a Task\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of use - List tasks\nSetting up a Neaktor webhook\nNote\n\nOnly the account owner or a user with administrator rights can create webhooks in Neaktor.\n\nIn your Make scenario, select the Neaktor Watch Tasks module.\n\nUnder Webhook, click Add.\n\nGive your new webhook a name, then select the connection you want to use.\n\nClick Save.\n\nCopy the webhook URL address to your clipboard.\n\nLog in to your Neaktor account.\n\nClick the plus icon at the top of the page, then click Integration.\n\nClick Webhooks.\n\nClick Add Webhook.\n\nGive your webhook a anme in the box provided.\n\nEnter the webhook URL in the Callback URL box.\n\nConfigure the rest of you webhook how you would like.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully set up the webhook.\n\nNeaktor\nConnect Neaktor to Make\nTasks\nWatch Tasks\nSearch Tasks\nGet a Task\nCreate a Task\nUpdate a Task\nDelete a Task\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of use - List tasks\nSetting up a Neaktor webhook\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

you to watch, create, update, retrieve, and delete the boards and widgets in your Miro account.\n\nTo get started with the Miro app, create an account at miro.com/signup.\n\nRefer to the Miro API Documentation for the list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Miro to Make\nNote\n\nThe Miro app allows only one connection for one user. You will receive an error if you try to create a second connection with the same user details. You need to delete any existing user connection before creating a new one.\n\nTo establish the connection:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add any Miro module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional: Click Show Advanced Settings and enter your client credentials and team ID from your custom app.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm the access.\n\nYou have successfully connected the Miro app with Make and can now build scenarios.\n\nBuild Miro Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nBoards\n\nWatch Boards\n\nCreate a Board\n\nNote: If you receive an insufficient permissions error when creating a board, see the Troubleshooting section.\n\nCopy a Board\n\nUpdate a Board\n\nList Boards\n\nGet a Board\n\nItems\n\nWatch Items\n\nCreate a Shape Item\n\nList Items\n\nGet an Item\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nTroubleshooting\n\nInsufficient permissions when creating a board:\n\nDescription: When creating a board using Create a Board module in Make, receiving the error message, Insufficient permissions to perform operation. Please check the permissions or contact support.\n\nWorkaround: Modify user-specific policy settings and permissions in your Miro account settings as shown in the below images.\n\nMiro\nConnect Miro to Make\nBuild Miro Scenarios\nTroubleshooting\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Nozbe Teams modules in Make, you can manage the tasks and comments in your Nozbe account.\n\nTo use the Nozbe Teams modules, you must have a Nozbe account. You can create an account at nozbe.com.\n\nRefer to the Nozbe Teams API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Nozbe Teams to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Nozbe.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Nozbe\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Nozbe account:\n\nLog in to your Nozbe account.\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Settings icon > Settings.\n\nClick API tokens > Add new token.\n\nEnter a name for the token and click Add.\n\nCopy the API key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Token field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Nozbe Teams in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Nozbe Teams module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. in Make, you can retrieve, update, and watch column values, create, duplicate, retrieve, delete and/or list boards, groups, teams, users, items, updates, subscribers, and/or files, and execute GraphQL queries.\n\nTo get started with the Monday app, create an account at auth.monday.com/users/sign_up.\n\nRefer to the Monday API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Monday to Make\n\nTo connect Monday to Make, you must obtain an API Key from your Monday account.\n\nLog in to your Monday account.\n\nClick your profile icon > Admin.\n\nNavigate to the API section.\n\nTo use a new token, click Create a new API Token, copy the Personal API Token, and store it in a safe place.\n\nTo use an existing token, copy the Personal API Token and store it in a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Monday module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter Businessmap modules in Make, you can manage the cards, links, subtasks, comments, logged times, and workspaces in your Businessmap account.\n\nTo use the Businessmap modules, you must have a paid Businessmap account. You can create an account at businessmap.io/signup. For subscription information, refer to the Businessmap Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the Businessmap REST API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Businessmap to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Businessmap.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Businessmap\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Businessmap account:\n\nLog in to your Businessmap account.\n\nIn the top-right corner, click My Account > API.\n\nCopy the API key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Key field in Make.\n\nNote\n\nAt the time of this publication, all steps for Obtain your API Key in Businessmap were checked and verified to be accurate. However this may have changed, so please see the Businessmap Knowledge Base for the most up-to-date directions.\n\nEstablish the connection with Businessmap in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Businessmap module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Subdomain field, enter your account's subdomain. This is the first part of your Businessmap URL.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied in the section above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Businessmap modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Kanbanize Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nCards\n\nWatch Card Created\n\nWatch Card Updated\n\nWatch Card Moved\n\nCreate a Card\n\nUpdate a Card\n\nGet a Card\n\nList Cards\n\nLinks\n\nUpdate a Link\n\nList Linked Cards\n\nDelete a Link\n\nSubtasks\n\nCreate a Subtask\n\nUpdate a Subtask\n\nComments\n\nCreate a Comment\n\nLogged Times\n\nAdd a Logged Time to a Card\n\nWorkspaces\n\nList Workspaces\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nNote\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nWhen you create a Kanbanize webhook in Make, it is attached automatically and requires no additional set up.\n\nBusinessmap\nConnect Businessmap to Make\nObtain your API key in Businessmap\nEstablish the connection with Businessmap in Make\nBuild Kanbanize Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
